Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a condition where breathing is repeatedly interrupted during sleep.
  It is often caused by a blockage or narrowing of the airways.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma is a type of tumor that occurs in the jaw and can cause swelling and pain, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  A dentigerous cyst is a type of cyst that forms around an unerupted tooth, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  An orbital fracture is a break in the bones surrounding the eye, but it is not known to cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joint becomes fused, making it difficult to open the mouth. This can cause obstructive sleep apnoea due to the narrowing of the airway.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a condition in which breathing is repeatedly interrupted during sleep.
  It is caused by the blockage of the upper airway.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst are tumors that can cause jaw swelling, but they do not directly affect the airway.
  Orbital fracture is a fracture of the bones surrounding the eye, which can cause double vision, but it does not affect the airway.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is the fusion of the jawbone to the skull, which can cause severe restriction of jaw movement and difficulty opening the mouth.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis can cause obstruction of the upper airway and lead to obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.

Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has a history of myocardial infarction, which is a risk factor for cardiovascular disease.
  The lipid profile shows high triglycerides and low HDL cholesterol, which are also risk factors for cardiovascular disease.
  The goal of treatment is to reduce the risk of cardiovascular disease.
  Statins are the first-line therapy for reducing LDL cholesterol levels, which is elevated in this patient.
  Fibrates are effective in reducing triglyceride levels and increasing HDL cholesterol levels.
  Combination therapy with a statin and a fibrate may increase the risk of adverse effects.
  Therefore, the preferred treatment for this patient is a statin alone.
  Among the given options, Rosuvastatin 10 mg is the preferred treatment for this patient.
Action: Answer("C")

  Fibrates are used to lower TG levels and increase HDL levels.
  Combination therapy with statins and fibrates can be considered in patients with persistent hypertriglyceridemia and low HDL levels.
  Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose and may not be necessary for this patient.

  Based on the patient's lipid profile, combination therapy with Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate would be the best option.

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
  The third ventricle is a narrow cavity located in the midline of the brain.
  It lies between the two thalami and is continuous with the cerebral aqueduct.
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by the hypothalamus.
  The optic stalk and the infundibulum are part of the hypothalamus and are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  The third nerve also known as the oculomotor nerve is a cranial nerve that originates from the midbrain and passes through the lateral wall of the third ventricle.
  The mammillary body is located on the floor of the fourth ventricle and is not present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Mammillary body.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The third ventricle is a structure in the brain that is filled with cerebrospinal fluid.
  The floor of the third ventricle contains several structures, including the optic stalk, the infundibulum, and the mammillary body.
  The third nerve is not normally located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")

  The infundibulum is a funnel-shaped structure that connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus.
  The mammillary body is a pair of small round structures located on the undersurface of the brain.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of the third ventricle is the third nerve.

Topic: Dental
Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Thought:
  Pulpectomy and pulp capping are procedures performed to treat the pulp of a tooth.
  Primary teeth are also known as baby teeth.
  Baby teeth have different characteristics than adult teeth.
  Increased odontoblastic activity in the young means that the cells responsible for dentin formation are more active in primary teeth.
  Increased blood supply through the wide apex means that primary teeth have a wider opening at the tip of the root, allowing for more blood flow.
  Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth means that there is more pulp tissue in primary teeth.
  Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young means that there is less collagen in primary teeth.
  Based on this information, the most likely answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Pulpectomy is the removal of the entire pulp from the pulp chamber and root canal of a tooth.
  Pulp capping is a technique used in dental restorations to prevent the dental pulp from dying, after being exposed by a cavity or trauma.
  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that develop in children.
  Primary teeth have a shorter root and wider apex.
  Primary teeth have a larger pulp chamber and thinner dentin walls.
  Primary teeth have more odontoblasts, which are cells that form dentin.
  Therefore, the increased odontoblastic activity in primary teeth is the reason why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  The answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.

  B: Lymphatics

  D: Aspiration of tumor cells

Response 2:
Thought:
  Metastasis is the spread of cancer from one part of the body to another.
  Oral cancer is a type of cancer that can occur in any part of the mouth.
  The oral cavity has a rich lymphatic network.
  Lymphatic vessels are thin tubes that carry lymph, a clear fluid containing white blood cells, away from the body tissues and toward the bloodstream.
  Lymphatic vessels drain into lymph nodes, which are small, bean-shaped structures that help fight infection and disease.
  Cancer cells can break away from the primary tumor and travel through the lymphatic vessels to nearby lymph nodes.
  Therefore, the most common route for metastasis of oral cancer is through the lymphatics.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure to access the root surface of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres attach the cementum to the alveolar bone.
  If the root surface has been exposed for 6 years, it is likely that the PDL fibres have been lost.
  Therefore, the lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.
  The answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root of a tooth.
  Roots that have been denuded for a long time will have lost their periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres.
  In this case, the lateral sliding flap will show PDL fibres attached to cementum or dentin.
  The lateral sliding flap will not show epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
  Co adaptation to the remaining fibres is not a direct result of the lateral sliding flap.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves moving a flap of gum tissue to expose the underlying tooth root.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the tooth has been without gum tissue for 6 years.
  In this case, the PDL (periodontal ligament) fibres, which attach the tooth to the surrounding bone, will have been lost.
  Therefore, the lateral sliding flap will not show PDL fibres attached to cementum or dentin.

Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:
Thought:
  The density of lipoproteins increases as the protein content increases relative to lipid content.
  Chylomicrons are the largest and least dense lipoproteins.
  VLDL is denser than chylomicrons but less dense than LDL.
  LDL is denser than VLDL but less dense than HDL.
  HDL is the most dense lipoprotein.
  Therefore, the lipoprotein with the least density is Chylomicrons.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The density of lipoproteins is inversely proportional to their size.
  The larger the size of the lipoprotein, the less dense it is.
  Chylomicrons are the largest lipoproteins.
  Therefore, they have the least density.
  The answer is D: Chylomicrons.

- Therefore, the answer is D: Chylomicrons.

Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?
Choices:
  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  The Bishop score is used to assess the cervical status before induction of labor.
  The score ranges from 0 to 13.
  The higher the score, the more favorable the cervix is for induction.
  The components of the Bishop score are cervical dilation, effacement, station, consistency, and position.
  In this case, the patient's cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced, which gives a score of 1 for dilation and 2 for effacement.
  The station is -1, which gives a score of 0.
  The consistency is soft, which gives a score of 2.
  The position is posterior, which gives a score of 0.
  Adding the scores together, we get 1+2+0+2+0=5.
  Therefore, the modified Bishop score for this lady is 5.

Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:
  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Thought:
  Malocclusion is a condition that affects the alignment of teeth.
  Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population that have a specific condition at a given point in time.
  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a specific condition that occur in a population over a period of time.
  Morbidity refers to the incidence of disease in a population.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring.
  Since the question is asking about the proportion of individuals in a population that have a specific condition at a given point in time, the best answer is A: Prevalence rate.

  Morbidity refers to the incidence of disease in a population.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of a specific event occurring.

  Therefore, the best description of the occurrence of malocclusion in a given population is prevalence rate.

  A: DMT-1
  B: Ferropoin
  C: Transferrin
  D: Hepcidin

  Ferropoin is not a known transporter for iron uptake.
  Transferrin is a plasma protein that binds to iron and transports it to the cells.

  Thin flange means the part of the denture that extends towards the cheeks or lips is not thick enough to provide support.
  Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth means the denture is not covering enough surface area of the teeth, which can lead to instability.
  Defective occlusal balancing can cause premature contact and can lead to sore spots.
  Out of all the options, the most likely reason for looseness in a recently delivered RPD is a Passive clasp on abutment.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 8:
Thought:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  Looseness in RPD can be due to various reasons.
  Passive clasp on abutment means the clasp is not engaging the abutment properly.
  Thin flange can cause discomfort but not looseness.
  Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth can cause tipping of the denture.
  Defective occlusal balancing can cause the denture to dislodge during function.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Defective occlusal balancing.

  The excess GH leads to overgrowth of bones and tissues.
  Some of the clinical features of acromegaly include enlarged hands and feet, thickened skin, and coarsened facial features.
  A large tongue may also be a feature of acromegaly due to the overgrowth of soft tissues.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized, and it is not associated with acromegaly.
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly, but hyperglycemia (high blood sugar) may be seen due to insulin resistance.
  Crowded teeth may also be seen in acromegaly due to the overgrowth of facial bones.

Question: Which of the following is rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles is?
Choices:
  A: Glycolysis
  B: Glycogenolysis
  C: TCA cycle
  D: Phosphocreatine
Response 0:
Thought:
  The question is asking for a rapid source of energy for exercising muscles.
  Glycolysis and glycogenolysis are processes that break down glucose and glycogen respectively to produce ATP.
  The TCA cycle is a slower process that produces ATP from the breakdown of glucose and other molecules.
  Phosphocreatine is a molecule that can rapidly donate a phosphate group to ADP to resynthesize ATP.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Phosphocreatine.
Action: Answer("D")

  Phosphocreatine is a molecule that can donate a phosphate group to ADP to produce ATP.
  Phosphocreatine is a rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles.

Topic: Gynaecology & Obstetrics
Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a pregnancy complication characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs, often the kidneys.
  Proteinuria is a common symptom of preeclampsia.
  Severe preeclampsia is a serious condition that can cause organ damage and other complications.
  According to the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists (ACOG), proteinuria of 5 g or more in a 24-hour urine sample is one of the diagnostic criteria for severe preeclampsia.
  5 g is equivalent to 5000 mg.
  Therefore, the answer is not A, B, or C.
  The answer is D: 3000 mg.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Preeclampsia is a condition that occurs during pregnancy.
  It is characterized by high blood pressure and proteinuria.
  Severe preeclampsia is a serious condition that can lead to maternal and fetal complications.
  The level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia is usually greater than 300 mg in a 24-hour urine collection.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 300 mg.

  The semi-colon shaped C-shaped canal is classified as Type 3.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought:
  According to Melton and Seitzor, there are four types of C-shaped canals.
  Type 1: C-shaped canals with a single, continuous canal from orifice to apex.
  Type 2: C-shaped canals with two orifices and a single canal or two canals joining short of the apex.
  Type 3: C-shaped canals with two orifices and two canals joining short of the apex.
  Type 4: Semi-colon shaped C-shaped canals.

Topic: Biochemistry
Question: In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway. This is reflected by the accumulation of what substance in blood?
Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is a pathway that synthesizes heme, which is a component of hemoglobin, the molecule that carries oxygen in red blood cells.
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Uroporphyrinogen III, coproporphyrinogen III, protoporphyrin IX, and heme are the intermediates of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first intermediate of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Ferrochelatase is the enzyme that catalyzes the insertion of iron into protoporphyrin IX to form heme.
  Porphobinogen is a precursor of heme but not an intermediate of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Therefore, the substance that accumulates in blood due to inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway in lead poisoning is Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA).
Action: Answer("D")

  Delta amino levulinic acid (ALA) is the first compound in the heme biosynthetic pathway.

  Therefore, the answer is D: Delta amino levulinic acid.

  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin

- Repaglinide and Glimepiride are sulfonylureas and are not preferred in renal impairment.
- Therefore, the best option for this patient is either Linagliptin or Vildagliptin.
- Among the given options, only A and C are DPP-4 inhibitors.
- Therefore, the answer is either A: Linagliptin or C: Vildagliptin.

  Stratified random sampling is a method where the population is divided into subgroups and a random sample is taken from each subgroup.
  Cluster sampling is a method where the population is divided into clusters and a random sample of clusters is selected.
  The question is asking for a method that selects patients based on potential factors that will affect the results.
